  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_de3fdd94-9121-49bd-b24e-74341d862397'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/75971674-dennis-keithly"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1522937610i/75971674._UY100_CR1,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/75971674-dennis-keithly">Dennis Keithly</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I took it to be that she was furious over the invasion into Actis Tor to such a degree that she could not speak in such a way with her own voice so as<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I took it to be that she was furious over the invasion into Actis Tor to such a degree that she could not speak in such a way with her own voice so as to contain her power. When she snarled at Harry at the end of the book, even briefly, it injured him. Therefore, she used the Grimalkin to prevent herself from harming him.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_3091105993" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3091105993" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3091105993?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8123311-small-favor">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3091105993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16252757231633670845"><b>For better or worse, <i>Small Favor</i> is a fully action-packed packed—have I mentioned packed?—volume.</b><br/><br/>To the longtime fans of the series, here’s a brief reminder that <i>Peace talks</i>, the long-awaited sequel in <i>The Dresden Files</i> series, is out now! As for me, I’m still slowly catching up. I actually wish I can prolong my speed, but it seems likely that by October or November, I’ll be fully caught up with the series.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Punctuality is for people with nothing better to do.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>Just when he thought his</span>
  <span id="freeText16252757231633670845" style="display:none"><b>For better or worse, <i>Small Favor</i> is a fully action-packed packed—have I mentioned packed?—volume.</b><br><br>To the longtime fans of the series, here’s a brief reminder that <i>Peace talks</i>, the long-awaited sequel in <i>The Dresden Files</i> series, is out now! As for me, I’m still slowly catching up. I actually wish I can prolong my speed, but it seems likely that by October or November, I’ll be fully caught up with the series.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Punctuality is for people with nothing better to do.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Just when he thought his life is looking up, everything seems to be at peace, but then the past visits. Mab, the Queen of Air and Darkness, calls in an old favor from Harry Dresden, and immediately all hell breaks loose. There’s a lot going on here; Were-goats, the Archive, the Knights of the Cross, Marcone, Mab, and last but not least, Nicodemus and the Denarians. Suffice to say the life for Harry and his friends are imperiled once again. Small Favor, the tenth volume in the series, is an installment full of actions. If you’ve been following my reviews, you know how much I enjoyed reading <i>The Dresden Files</i>, but at the same time, you’re also probably sick of me criticizing the pacing of its action scenes in some volumes. Unfortunately, this novel by far the most action-packed volume of the series so far. There was almost no room for breathing, and this was especially true in the middle section of the book, and I have to say that it did bore me a bit.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Think of every fairy-tale villainess you've ever heard of. Think of the wicked witches, the evil queens, the mad enchantresses. Think of the alluring sirens, the hungry ogresses, the savage she-beasts. Think of them and remember that somewhere, sometime, they've all been real.<br><br>Mab gave them lessons.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>With this series, I definitely prefer when there are breaks and room for breathing rather than continuous actions. Butcher has an engaging and straightforward writing style, and the formulaic storytelling structure does make long action sequences boring because most of the time, we’ll know the result of the battles already. I love <i>The Dresden Files</i> more when the actions are spread out; as I said, the best part of <i>The Dresden Files</i> is when Butcher focusses the narrative on Harry and the development of his relationships with the important people in his life; that’s what Butcher did in the second half of Small Favor, and it worked really well for me.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Caring about someone isn't complicated. It isn't easy. But it isn't complicated, either. Kinda like lifting the engine block out of a car.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>We’re halfway through July now, and honestly, I’ve been having a rut of a reading month. So far, I’ve had two DNF, and the last three books I managed to finish were either disappointing or just okay. As a matter of fact, the last book that I enjoyed thoroughly was the previous installment to <i>Small Favor</i>: <i>White Night</i>. <i>Small Favor</i> brings back old enemies while developing the characterizations of the cast of characters further with engaging dialogues and cool action scenes. I’m pleased to once again add another book in <i>The Dresden Files</i> to the list of great books I read this month.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“You rush a miracle worker, you get lousy miracles!”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><b>Picture: <i>Small Favor</i> by Vincent Chong</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1594884065i/29821643._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>You can order the book from: <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9780356500362/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u></b><br><br><b>You can find <u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2020/07/16/book-review-small-favor-the-dresden-files-10-by-jim-butcher/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u> and the rest of my reviews at <u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b><br><br><i>Special thanks to my Patrons on <b><u><a href="https://www.patreon.com/petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Patreon</a></u></b> for giving me extra support towards my passion for reading and reviewing!<br><br>My Patrons: Alfred, Alya, Annabeth, Devin, Hamad, Jimmy Nutts, Joie, Mike, Miracle, Nicholas, Zoe.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16252757231633670845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1827586934" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1827586934" />
    <a title="Paul O&#39;Neill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17331573-paul-o-neill"><img alt="Paul O&#39;Neill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462480730p2/17331573.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1827586934?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul O&#39;Neill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul O&#39;Neill" href="/user/show/17331573-paul-o-neill">Paul O&#39;Neill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1827586934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6686589445249353208">Hell’s bells, this series just keeps on getting better and better!!<br/><br/>During a blizzard in Chicago, yellow page advertising wizard Harry Dresden is summoned by the queen of Winter, Mab, who calls in a favour she is owed. The Denarians are back and they are the main foes in this story. The book also features Gruffs (as in the brothers Gruff, referred to by Harry as “were-goats”), the Archive, Marcone and the Knights of the cross. <br/><br/>This book is one of the deeper books in the series. It asks some quest</span>
  <span id="freeText6686589445249353208" style="display:none">Hell’s bells, this series just keeps on getting better and better!!<br /><br />During a blizzard in Chicago, yellow page advertising wizard Harry Dresden is summoned by the queen of Winter, Mab, who calls in a favour she is owed. The Denarians are back and they are the main foes in this story. The book also features Gruffs (as in the brothers Gruff, referred to by Harry as “were-goats”), the Archive, Marcone and the Knights of the cross. <br /><br />This book is one of the deeper books in the series. It asks some questions about right and wrong. I was welling up when Harry starts shouting at God in the church.<br /><br /><b>Format</b><br /><br />Book format: Audiobook narrated by James Marsters<br />Length: 13hrs 46mins<br />Difficulty: Easy<br />POV characters: One – Harry Dresden<br />Person: First<br />Chronology: Linear<br /><br />Butcher’s writing makes the book easy to digest and the fact that it’s told through Harry’s point of view makes it really easy to follow. <br /><br /><b>Characters</b><br /><br />Butcher has created a bunch of characters that I’ve grown very fond of. They have all developed through the course of the series and I love the fact that there isn’t a reset at the end of these books. The characters and the world is always different which gives each book a sense of purpose and they all add to the larger storyline. <br /><br />Dresden’s abilities are really growing and he always learns something new. In book one, his magic is still being worked on but they are almost epic here at book ten. Dresden has to be one of the coolest, and yet most human characters out there. <br /><br /><b>Writing</b><br /><br />The writing does its job, it takes you through the action, explains the magic and the world very clearly and transports you from A to B. Its very humorous, there are tonnes of laugh out loud moments that fans of the series have come to expect. <br /><br /><i>Likeith thou jelly within thy donut?</i><br /><br /><i>Sanity invited shame over for tea and biscuits</i><br /><br /><i>You rush a miracle worker, you get lousy miracles</i><br /><br /><i>We’re ostriches and the whole world is sand</i><br /><br /><b>Final thought</b> <br /><br />I’d say this series is a great place for anyone who’s looking to start reading. It’s simply the coolest, most fun, kick ass, character driven series there is. Butcher does a great job of explaining and recapping things so you don’t really need to read it in order, but I’d recommend you pick it up from the start. <br /><br />This is one of my favourite series ever and the audiobooks are just fantastic. Can’t recommend it highly enough.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6686589445249353208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_21095055" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21095055" />
    <a title="Reed" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1113585-reed"><img alt="Reed" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343239073p2/1113585.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21095055?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reed" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reed" href="/user/show/1113585-reed">Reed</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21095055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1557210289718395117">As I began reading the 10th Harry Dresden novel, I started ticking off little mental bullet points:<br/><br/>Sarcastic dialogue. <br/><br/>Harry in more trouble than any 3 urban fantasy characters.<br/><br/>The frenzied "first climax" that always happens in the middle of a Dresden novel.<br/><br/>Repetitive info-dumping (description of Harry's beat up Volkswagen, Mouse the huge-ass dog, his big-ass cat, his pretty-boy vampire brother, his burned hand, his terrible youth, the tavern for supernaturals . . . you get the point)<br/><br/>I began to </span>
  <span id="freeText1557210289718395117" style="display:none">As I began reading the 10th Harry Dresden novel, I started ticking off little mental bullet points:<br /><br />Sarcastic dialogue. <br /><br />Harry in more trouble than any 3 urban fantasy characters.<br /><br />The frenzied "first climax" that always happens in the middle of a Dresden novel.<br /><br />Repetitive info-dumping (description of Harry's beat up Volkswagen, Mouse the huge-ass dog, his big-ass cat, his pretty-boy vampire brother, his burned hand, his terrible youth, the tavern for supernaturals . . . you get the point)<br /><br />I began to wonder if I've grown weary of Butcher's series at this point. With all the, dare I say it, recycling of characters and plot points, Small Favor feels like "been there, done that. We have Marcone messing with things, The Winter and Summer Courts causing Harry trouble, Michael the Knight and Thomas the Vamp. It feels like Butcher is coasting a little bit.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, Small Favor is still enjoyable. If you like the Dresden series, it should satisfy that Harry Dresden itch. But I wish Butcher would mix it up a little bit more. He's beginning to do so, with Harry's Warden duties, his apprenticing of Molly, and so forth. I just wish he'd jump further away from his safe plot lines and venture into new territory.<br /><br />I'll still read the next Dresden novel. I love Harry, I like the dialog, and the writing is just plain fun. And I must admit, the last third of the book really picked up the action, and felt a bit more than going through the motions. I just hope the next novel wanders farther from the norm.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1557210289718395117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16850039525477240118">This was another action packed Harry Dresden adventure. Started off a little slow but sure did build momentum through the middle culminating in a massive battle. Harry is growing smarter and more powerful but is still young in wizarding terms especially when some heavy weight foes are out to get him. <br/>In this episode Mab, Queen of the Winter Court calls in a favour Harry owes her and asks him to rescue crime boss Marcone, who has been kidnapped by a bunch of fallen angels (called the Denarians). </span>
  <span id="freeText16850039525477240118" style="display:none">This was another action packed Harry Dresden adventure. Started off a little slow but sure did build momentum through the middle culminating in a massive battle. Harry is growing smarter and more powerful but is still young in wizarding terms especially when some heavy weight foes are out to get him. <br />In this episode Mab, Queen of the Winter Court calls in a favour Harry owes her and asks him to rescue crime boss Marcone, who has been kidnapped by a bunch of fallen angels (called the Denarians). At the same time Titania, Queen of the Summer Court is trying to stop Harry from rescuing Marcone and sends some fae creatures to hunt him down, including the brothers Gruff (you can imagine what they look like - each brother bigger than the one before). Fortunately Harry has his apprentice Molly, brother Thomas, a vampire and friend Michael, a knight of the Cross to watch his back and eventually the Wizard's White Council send in some Wizards to help. <br />What I love most about this series are not only the great characters and sheer inventiveness but also the humour in some of the scenes and witty repartee between Harry and the bad guys. I have a feeling this episode is setting the scene for more serious business to come, particularly if the Red and White Vampire Courts restart hostilities. I guess I shall just have to read on to find out!</span>

<div id="review_2911960944" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2911960944?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2911960944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16769683570686201499">When Mab, the faerie queen of the Winter Court, asks you for a small favor – it’s not really a small favor. Like Ron Burgundy it’s kind of a big deal.<br/><br/>So begins Jim Butcher’s TENTH Harry Dresden novel. The past few stories have been about Harry’s conflicts with vampires, especially the White Court. That problem having been more or less resolved for the time being, we now switch themes back to the faerie courts and a visit from the White Queen.<br/><br/>And getting saddled up on the WINTER side of the Fae m</span>
  <span id="freeText16769683570686201499" style="display:none">When Mab, the faerie queen of the Winter Court, asks you for a small favor – it’s not really a small favor. Like Ron Burgundy it’s kind of a big deal.<br><br>So begins Jim Butcher’s TENTH Harry Dresden novel. The past few stories have been about Harry’s conflicts with vampires, especially the White Court. That problem having been more or less resolved for the time being, we now switch themes back to the faerie courts and a visit from the White Queen.<br><br>And getting saddled up on the WINTER side of the Fae means he’s on the WRONG side of Titania, the Queen of the Summer Court. Harry just cannot stay out of trouble.<br><br>Three Billy Goats Gruff. Butcher has some fun with a tie in to the old fairy tale, these are some of the Summer Court minions come to tackle Harry.<br><br>But wait! There’s more! Besides Winter Court weirdness and Summer Court minion advances, the Denarians show up in full force and are back to stir up more hellish trouble. For readers who don’t know these are fallen angels bound to 30 pieces of silver who possess those who carry them. A cool idea for demonic bad guys.<br><br>Michael Carpenter, paladin. Is he a paladin? I think so, technically according to the story he’s a Knight of the Cross, but I imagine him as a paladin in the D&amp;D sense. And remember: Lawful Good does not mean lawful nice. He’s Old Testament BADASS in a fight, especially against supernatural goonies.<br><br>We also get to visit with The Archive, Kincaid, Gard and another trip to McAnally’s Pub. Good fun for Dresden fans.<br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1582479366i/29009572.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="16769683570686201499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51380085" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/51380085?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51380085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9377069652955840150">I was blown away by White Knight and couldn't possibly imagine this series getting any better than that. I'm happy to say Butcher may have done so. If anything, Small Favor's at least on the same level with what I already considered the best in the series. <br/><br/>Maybe I'm drinking the kool-aid at 10 books in, but this series has gotten much less annoying to me as it's progressed. I didn't notice too many over-explanations in this installment that drove me nuts about the first couple books in the serie</span>
  <span id="freeText9377069652955840150" style="display:none">I was blown away by White Knight and couldn't possibly imagine this series getting any better than that. I'm happy to say Butcher may have done so. If anything, Small Favor's at least on the same level with what I already considered the best in the series. <br /><br />Maybe I'm drinking the kool-aid at 10 books in, but this series has gotten much less annoying to me as it's progressed. I didn't notice too many over-explanations in this installment that drove me nuts about the first couple books in the series. I get that he's writing each installment to be its own separate story, which works for the most part, but it gets tiring and I'm glad that seems to be going away or severely reduced.<br /><br />Having said that, I don't think much more needs to be said. Butcher is really going deep in his world-building, adding more to each installment, while bringing up past characters/races. It's really getting wide and deep and it's exciting to see more and more of this world open up. Again, I realize I'm drinking the kool-aid at 10 books under my belt.<br /><br />Speaking of which, the Harry Dresden/James Marsters narration combo is just about the best thing known to fiction. I think I really started falling in love with the series when I started the audiobooks around book 6. <br /><br />4.5 out of 5 Stars (highly super duper recommended)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9377069652955840150" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_25051266" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/25051266" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/858949-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1208350750p2/858949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/25051266?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/858949-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/858949-chris?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/858949-chris?shelf=wizardry">wizardry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer25051266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer174405781997107748"><b>"Hell's Bells" count: 21</b><br/><br/>This is the tenth book in the series, and if Butcher's own plan can be trusted, it marks about the halfway point for the series as a whole. Having made it this far with the series is a remarkable achievement, and if he can keep it up all the way to its projected end, I will be a very happy and impressed reader. So, a few words about the book itself, and then some thoughts on the series.<br/><br/>Honestly, if you've been following my reviews of this series, you can be pretty sure wh</span>
  <span id="freeText174405781997107748" style="display:none"><b>"Hell's Bells" count: 21</b><br /><br />This is the tenth book in the series, and if Butcher's own plan can be trusted, it marks about the halfway point for the series as a whole. Having made it this far with the series is a remarkable achievement, and if he can keep it up all the way to its projected end, I will be a very happy and impressed reader. So, a few words about the book itself, and then some thoughts on the series.<br /><br />Honestly, if you've been following my reviews of this series, you can be pretty sure what I'm going to say about it - I devoured the book and enjoyed every minute of it. In this edition, Our Hero Harry is faced with death and danger on all sides, as usual. The everlasting Queen of the Winter Sidhe, Mab, wants Harry to rescue John Marcone, the boss of the biggest organized crime racket in the city, from the clutches of fallen angels who have immeasurable power and millennia of experience. What they want with Marcone - and other, more innocent and tragic characters - isn't clear, but what can can be sure of is that the full extent of their plans will far exceed simple kidnapping. <br /><br />Meanwhile, he's being attacked by agents of Queen Titania, the queen of the Summer Sidhe, for reasons that are not all that clear to anyone, especially Harry. His attackers are beasts of legend - the Gruffs. You may have heard of them when you were a child - goatlike creatures with a talent for eliminating trolls. They are brothers, and if you manage to defeat one of them, you can be sure that his big brother will be along soon to take care of you. And you most certainly don't want to get on the bad side of the eldest of the Gruffs, let me tell you that. Nice guy, but he's clean your clock no matter who you are.<br /><br />So, things aren't so good for Harry Dresden. But, then, when are they ever? Going up against forces way over his head is pretty much a theme for Harry's life, and while we can be reasonably certain that he will prevail (after all, there are about ten more books to go, and they'd be hard to write without him), we don't know how much damage he will take in the doing so. Although if you guessed "a lot," you'd be pretty well on the mark.<br /><br />That goes for pretty much every book in the series. Harry is an underdog, or at least he starts out as one. By the time you get to this book, he has some measure of authority, responsibility and respect, as well as a serious reputation amongst people in this world and others. So, this makes it rather harder for him to be an underdog. Instead of simple vampires, werewolves and the occasional necromancer, we now have to deal with the Big Guns like Mab, Titania and The Fallen. Which brings me to my first prediction for the rest of the series. <br /><br /><b>Harry Laid Low.</b> At some point, I figure all that he's built up will have to come crashing down. Gross physical harm aside, he's put himself in a much better position than the one he was in way back in <i>Storm Front</i>, and if he continues the way he has, he will cease to be the underdog and become the overdog, if there is such a thing. While it'll be interesting to see how he handles being higher up on the food chain, I don't think it'll sit well with his character.<br /><br />That would be unfortunate, because it's Harry's character that really make this book. I've talked to those who aren't too keen on investing in this series because it's not quite different enough from the other modern, urban fantasy out there. And in a way, they're right. A lone wolf investigator with a mysterious past and unknowable potential who has a talent for making big enemies? That could either be this series or the <i>Nightside</i> books by Simon Green, and I'm sure there's a few more that follow a similar pattern. Butcher isn't breaking open new ground with this series, at least not as far as I can tell. And a main character who is a wizard named Harry with a mysterious destiny and a tragic past? Yeah, like I'm sure you haven't thought of it already. I don't think that's Butcher's fault, though. Harry seems to be the kind of character who shows up in a writer's head long before the book gets published, and Gary Dresden or Fred Dresden doesn't sound as good.<br /><br />Though Christopher Dresden has a nice ring to it, I must say. Why aren't there more fictional heroes named Chris, anyway? Weird.<br /><br />Back on topic - what Butcher has done, and what makes me enjoy this series so much, is take the genre and populate it with really interesting people. One of the things I enjoy so much about Harry is that he seems to be someone I'd like to hang out with - he has a sense of humor that I enjoy, and seeing how many of my friends tend towards wise-assery, I think we'd get along well. Other characters, like Murphy, Michael, Molly (lots of M names), Thomas, Bob, Mouse.... They're complex, they're interesting and occasionally surprising. You really come to care about them, because Harry cares about them and you care about Harry.<br /><br />Which reminds me: Predictions 2 and 3 - <b>The Death of Karrin Murphy</b> and <b>The Corruption of Molly Carpenter</b>. These are two people who are extremely close to Harry, and invoke his much-debated sense of male chauvinism. A few people seem to take issue with Harry's desire to protect women, which appears hopelessly old-fashioned. Maybe it is, but Harry (and by extension Butcher) seems to be okay with that. Murphy is Harry's best friend, the one character who's stood by him since the first book, and has grown to be his closest ally. She has gained his trust and his faith through fire and trial, and in this book is actually able to assert her authority (in a wonderful, wonderful scene) to save Harry's skin.<br /><br />So, she has to die. It's one of those Hero's Journey things - the hero has to lose those things closest to him in order to come out the other side as a True Hero. He needs Murphy, he really does, and he needs to be able to stand without her. If that means that she's taken out, well.... I don't know if or when it'll happen - I'd bet somewhere in the climactic final books.<br /><br />As for Molly, she's an interesting person. A young person who, after a very rocky start to her life as a magic-user, has been given a second chance by Harry. For his part, Harry's job is to make sure she turns out right, to make sure she learns how to use her powers responsibly and wisely, for the betterment of others. As of this book, she's doing very well - her powers are becoming more refined, and she's got a good handle on what it means to be a responsible wizard.<br /><br />But first, she has to see her dark side, look it in the eye, and face it down. So, at some point, Molly is going to slip. Whether through impatience, arrogance or circumstance, she's going to risk both her and Harry's lives by using her powers for Evil.<br /><br />There you go, then. It's a great series, very enjoyable, and I'll be following it to the end. I highly recommend you do the same.</span>
  <a data-text-id="174405781997107748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2424477900828621978" style="display:none">When Mab, the Winter Queen, comes to cash in on one of the favors Harry owes her, things go from bad to worse. And snow won't stop falling on Chicago. Could the two possibly be related?<br /><br /><i>Instinct told me that reason had disappointed me more than once, and that it wasn't thinking in the long term anyway. Over the years, my instincts and I have gotten cozy.</i> pg 57, ebook.<br /><br />Memorable characters from the previous entries in <i>The Dresden Files</i> make a reappearance in this, the tenth book in the series. We get to enjoy the company of Toot-Toot (the pizza-loving pixie), "gentleman" Johnny Marcone and Mab, among others.<br /><br /><i>Our instincts were a long time in the making, though, and the threats that can come after us now have outpaced them. You can't outrun a bullet, and you don't go hand-to-hand with a gunman unless you're certain you are about to die anyway.</i> pg 79, ebook.<br /><br />There's also a major villain from Harry's past, but I won't go into details and spoil it for you.<br /><br /><i>At one time in my life, a shapeshifted, demonically possessed maniac crashing through a window and trying to rip my face off would have come as an enormous and nasty surprise. But that time was pretty much in the past.</i> pg 143, ebook.<br /><br />I have read a few reviews in which some readers believe <i>The Dresden Files</i> is ridiculous because Jim Butcher puts Harry into situations that he couldn't possibly survive. But I beg to differ. As the stakes and bad guys increase, so do Harry's friends and allies. Yes, perhaps the wizard from book one would have been crushed by the baddie in book ten, but they're both at different places now.<br /><br />Dare I say it... Harry has "learned" things? Through his nearly constant trials and tribulations, he's become a stronger magic user, more adept and emphatic? But no, that may be going a bit too far.<br /><br /><i>The prime rule of combat wizardry is simple too: Be prepared.</i> pg 143, ebook.<br /><br />At least he's nailed down his wardrobe game...<br /><br /><i>Going forth to do battle with the forces of darkness is one thing. Doing it in a pair of borrowed sweatpants and an ill-fitting T-shirt is something else entirely.</i> pg 427, ebook.<br /><br />One final thought, in the other books in this series, I felt like things were getting worse and worse for our intrepid hero. But, as readers discover in this entry, there may be a silver lining on all those clouds after all.<br /><br />And all I have to say about that is: it's about time!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2424477900828621978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1343238303" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1343238303" />
    <a title="Luffy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7407364-luffy"><img alt="Luffy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606210775p2/7407364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1343238303?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luffy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luffy" href="/user/show/7407364-luffy">Luffy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=dresden">dresden</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1343238303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3995203290261137358">Giving a book 5 stars doesn't mean it's perfect. It's just that though I use it with a discriminative, fair, and remunerative sense of dosage, I know there are 2 farcical sides to this particular coin. First, for how long do I wait before ceding to impulse and rate a book 5 stars. Secondly, what do I do if, a week after giving Small Favor 5 stars, I chance on a book 10 times better? Cheerfully, those issues are non sequitur in my mind. Small Favor began slowly, embracing its pulpish roots and fl</span>
  <span id="freeText3995203290261137358" style="display:none">Giving a book 5 stars doesn't mean it's perfect. It's just that though I use it with a discriminative, fair, and remunerative sense of dosage, I know there are 2 farcical sides to this particular coin. First, for how long do I wait before ceding to impulse and rate a book 5 stars. Secondly, what do I do if, a week after giving Small Favor 5 stars, I chance on a book 10 times better? Cheerfully, those issues are non sequitur in my mind. Small Favor began slowly, embracing its pulpish roots and fleshing out its friendly universe where beings thrive even in places called Nevernever. I thought the musings of the Dresden Files, which earned my respect and interest by hitting on core metaphysical ideas, has been impotently pruned, in Small Favor, down to self help level. However, I underestimated Jim Butcher, and from the middle of the book to the twist of the last step, I was regaled with rich storytelling of the like that am grateful for. Definitely 5 star material.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3995203290261137358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8386404-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351707681p2/8386404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1408500728?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/8386404-richard">Richard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841496887" href="/book/show/3503263-small-favour">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386404-richard?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1408500728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15237031002027583091">8.5/10<br/><br/>Easily in the top 3 of the Dresden Files series and I’d go as far to say it’s my second favourite unable to pip Dead Beat by just a fraction (minus a star for no Polka music). The whole book was just fun to read, maybe it was the snowy Chicago setting and reading this over Christmas and the lack of snow provided by the weird British weather systems here. That’s a disservice though as there is so much going on in this book that it was hard to put this down and I was hooked up until the fina</span>
  <span id="freeText15237031002027583091" style="display:none">8.5/10<br /><br />Easily in the top 3 of the Dresden Files series and I’d go as far to say it’s my second favourite unable to pip Dead Beat by just a fraction (minus a star for no Polka music). The whole book was just fun to read, maybe it was the snowy Chicago setting and reading this over Christmas and the lack of snow provided by the weird British weather systems here. That’s a disservice though as there is so much going on in this book that it was hard to put this down and I was hooked up until the final sentence. <br /><br />One thing that may have been a stroke of luck was that I listened to book 5, Death Masks, in the series which had many re-occurring plot points and characters in this book so these were nice and fresh in my mind. Things do get explained in the book to backfill which can be quite annoying at times, its book 10 of the series. I know Dresden is a wizard by now and that certain characters are linked to Harry. Sometimes it is handy as there have been 10 books and I’m not reading back to back so I do forget certain plot points so I can let the re-caps slide.<br /><br />I won’t reveal anything related to the plot as there would be some spoilers to things earlier in the series but there are some really good action scenes in this one with at least 3 specifically that spring to mind which had me figuratively on the edge of my seat. One scene specifically made me carry on reading until the book was finished even though it was way past my bedtime which shows how much I was into this book. <br /><br />The series continues to impress, 10 books in and I’m happy that I’ve still got a fair amount to go at. Jim Butcher manages to keep things interesting and unique enough in each book to make me want to grab the next one but also links them enough to make you care about the characters and what is going to happen to them and what is going to happen in the next outing. This is fast becoming one of my favourite series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15237031002027583091" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2616526700" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12932355801588500026">WOW. <b>
  <i>Small Favor</i>
</b> was another epic read in the <i>Dresden Files</i> series. Harry is in deep again.<br/><br/>After <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/91475.White_Night__The_Dresden_Files___9_' title='White Night (The Dresden Files, #9) by Jim Butcher' rel='nofollow noopener'>White Night</a>, Harry has had some time to spend with his brother, friends, and his young apprentice, but now all that’s changing. <br/><br/>We have intrigue, betrayal, action-packed moments, and some surprises along the way.<br/><br/>Their’s a game a foot and lots of secrets. Molly, Thomas, Murphy, the Knights of the Cross, and Kincaid join Harry on this adventure. We also get the Billy Goat Gruff, Dark Magic, Summer </span>
  <span id="freeText12932355801588500026" style="display:none">WOW. <b>
  <i>Small Favor</i>
</b> was another epic read in the <i>Dresden Files</i> series. Harry is in deep again.<br><br>After <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/91475.White_Night__The_Dresden_Files___9_" title="White Night (The Dresden Files, #9) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">White Night</a>, Harry has had some time to spend with his brother, friends, and his young apprentice, but now all that’s changing. <br><br>We have intrigue, betrayal, action-packed moments, and some surprises along the way.<br><br>Their’s a game a foot and lots of secrets. Molly, Thomas, Murphy, the Knights of the Cross, and Kincaid join Harry on this adventure. We also get the Billy Goat Gruff, Dark Magic, Summer trying to kill Harry, and Mab calling in an old favor. <br><br>Now, Harry only really has one option when it comes to Mab and it’s not the best, but it’s the lesser of the evils. I really loved having the gang together again. I liked that his friend have his back, even if it’s in question, they still stick by him. Bob, the talking skull always adds humor and I love seeing him. Harry finally learns something about “Fidelacchiu,” one for the swords of God, that he is holding on too and hasn’t given to anyone yet. We also see The Fallen and The Archive. <br><br>WOW! Just WOW! So much happens in Small Favor and it’s gripping. Butcher brings out the changes that are happening with Harry and around him. There where also some very emotional intense scenes and pivotal plot twists.<br><br><b>
  <i>Small Favor</i>
</b> was another stellar read in this series. I have no idea what’s next for Harry and the gang, but I’m looking forward to continue the adventure. <br><br><b>Rated: 4.5 Stars</b><br><br><a href="http://angelsguiltypleasures.com" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_1978073557" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1978073557" />
    <a title="HBalikov" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/929238-hbalikov"><img alt="HBalikov" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271764879p2/929238.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1978073557?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1978073557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16957092782397633378">My intention is to keep this review short since many of you already know that I consider Jim Butcher’s Dresden series one of the finest collections of contemporary fantasy writing…and because I want to avoid any spoilers for those of you who have yet to read Small Favor. <br/><br/>In this novel, there is plenty of action and Butcher keeps it going with imaginative variations. Harry finds that he is over his head almost right from the start and has to call on a large number of his allies in order to solve </span>
  <span id="freeText16957092782397633378" style="display:none">My intention is to keep this review short since many of you already know that I consider Jim Butcher’s Dresden series one of the finest collections of contemporary fantasy writing…and because I want to avoid any spoilers for those of you who have yet to read Small Favor. <br /><br />In this novel, there is plenty of action and Butcher keeps it going with imaginative variations. Harry finds that he is over his head almost right from the start and has to call on a large number of his allies in order to solve the underlying mystery of what has happened to Chicago’s number one crime boss. This becomes important because Harry has to pay a debt to Queen Mab of the Winter Court and that “small favor” leads to a conflict that threatens Earth as we know it. <br /><br />For those of you who have read none of the Harry Dresden series, be aware that Harry is all that is keeping those other worlds of magic and demons from destroying the life that you hold dear. Harry works from Chicago and pays the bills by hiring out as a private investigator. He uses his skills (in white magic) as part of his investigations and his investigations usually come to involve the “supernatural.”<br /><br /> More than some of the books in this series, Small Favor drags in elements of the White Court, the Red Court, the Black Court, the Summer Court and the Winter Court. These are terms I won’t explain in detail except to say that we are given a fully developed alternate world with characters who interact in ways that may or may not affect the plot. There are those who say they are on the side of good, and those who say that they serve some other goal and those who are just out for anything they can get. They may be ghouls, vampires, pixies or succubae. Harry has powers, some of them pretty awesome, but there are costs to using them and costs to resisting their use. We find out a lot more about the balance of power as Harry Dresden must counter the challenge posed by the Danarians led by Nicodemus.<br /><br />As I said earlier, there is plenty of non-stop action, and when you think it might be over, it isn’t. What may impress me most beyond the excellent writing is that Butcher keeps track of everything (like a professional juggler). There may have been something that occurred three or five books ago, but he has not lost track of it and blends it seamlessly into the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16957092782397633378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11522923181743905207" style="display:none">I recently realized I didn't give this book a real review last time. So i will today!<br /><br />I'm weird about audiobooks. I can't listen to a book I've never read, but I also get kind of bored listening to books I've already read. Weird situation. <div id="review_22132151" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/22132151" />
    <a title="Seth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63444-seth"><img alt="Seth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1187495654p2/63444.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/22132151?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seth" href="/user/show/63444-seth">Seth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63444-seth?shelf=modernfantasy">modernfantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63444-seth?shelf=sf-f-h">sf-f-h</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22132151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12223235802336796883">About 1/4 into <u>Small Favor</u> I found myself wondering if Harry Dresden was about to magically jump a shark. By the end, I had decided it might be the best book in the series. <br/><br/>Well, he actually does kind of jump a shark, but he was in an aquarium at the time.<br/><br/><u>Favor</u> put us firmly back in Dresden's home territory. Someone has kidnapped his least-favorite sometimes-ally "Gentleman" Marcone and he's being coerced into saving him by an old enemy. His allies in faerie-land are trying to kill him. His frie</span>
  <span id="freeText12223235802336796883" style="display:none">About 1/4 into <u>Small Favor</u> I found myself wondering if Harry Dresden was about to magically jump a shark. By the end, I had decided it might be the best book in the series. <br /><br />Well, he actually does kind of jump a shark, but he was in an aquarium at the time.<br /><br /><u>Favor</u> put us firmly back in Dresden's home territory. Someone has kidnapped his least-favorite sometimes-ally "Gentleman" Marcone and he's being coerced into saving him by an old enemy. His allies in faerie-land are trying to kill him. His friend Michael is seriously doubting whether Harry is trustworthy. And he winds up stuck in the convergence of conflicts between the Seelie and Unseelie courts and between the Knights of the Cross and the Denarian demons. And just for fun, with Kincaid and Sergeant Murphy along for the ride, still bristling from their breakup.<br /><br />Thematically, this book is about divided loyalties, trust, and--most centrally--what it means to be good instead of evil. The central morals of Harry, Sergeant Murphy, Michael, Sanyo (another Knight of the Cross), and even the mercenaries Kincaid and Gard are roughly similar, but each draws different lines around what is required and what is allowed to be good. <br /><br />Marcone and The Archive (a super-efficent magical database of all written knowledge ever, but housed in a little girl) serve as the background to the moral debate: Marcone's morality is strongly personal, running his criminal empire and ruining whatever lives it costs while still going out of his way to save and help individuals he sees in distress. The Archive is impersonal, fighting to keep emotional attachments from driving her insane while she hold humanity's heritage against any disaster. They are each afraid to join human society fully, worried that they won't be able to reconcile their job with their humanity.<br /><br />The book is back in classic Dresden form in other ways, too. Harry doesn't rely on odd moments of insight that come like deus ex machina in some of the other books. He doesn't build plans that last longer than a day. And he doesn't ever rely on his intelligence over his wit, his wits, and his ability to break things very, very well. He's good at mouthing off, pushing people into making mistakes, and doing not-subtle magic with collateral damage. And he has charisma and leadership only Murphy can match. In <u>Small Favor</u> he leaves the other stuff to the pros. Just like the good old days.<br /><br />In a lot of ways, this is what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47212.Storm_Front__The_Dresden_Files___1_" title="Storm Front (The Dresden Files, #1) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Storm Front</a> would have been if Butcher had been a better writer at the time. It has more complex character interactions than the first book in a series can sustain and it assumes some (but not too much) knowledge of the backstory, but it hits the themes of the series without sacrificing the action and faith in himself that make Harry who he is. <br />.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12223235802336796883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13461887915262050272">Small Favor is the 10th book in The Dresden Files series by Jim Butcher. Harry Dresden is a wizard living in Chicago. Occasionally he helps out the local police with supernatural incidents and he hires on to help clients with hard-hitting magical problems. This time, he's in trouble.....a heavy hitter from the Winter Court calls in a favor. Whenever Mab wants something, it's always horrific and incredibly dangerous. What appears to be a kidnapping case ends up involving fallen angels, grotesque </span>
  <span id="freeText13461887915262050272" style="display:none">Small Favor is the 10th book in The Dresden Files series by Jim Butcher. Harry Dresden is a wizard living in Chicago. Occasionally he helps out the local police with supernatural incidents and he hires on to help clients with hard-hitting magical problems. This time, he's in trouble.....a heavy hitter from the Winter Court calls in a favor. Whenever Mab wants something, it's always horrific and incredibly dangerous. What appears to be a kidnapping case ends up involving fallen angels, grotesque supernatural goats and more. Another great urban fantasy action-packed book in this series!<br /><br />My husband has read all the books, including Brief Cases that just released this summer, and I want to catch up before the new book comes out. There is no publication date for Peace Talks yet, so I have time....but I want to have plenty of discussion time with hubby before the new book. Plus, I want to finish the series so far before he accidentally blurts out some important plot point accidentally. The struggle against spoilers is real, folks. :) <br /><br />I listened to the audio book version of this story. Loved it! James Marsters narrates. As I listened I knew I recognized the voice but couldn't quite place it....so I googled him. Marsters played Spike on Buffy! That fact made me enjoy his performance even more. :) I have hearing loss, but was easily able to hear and understand the entire book. Marsters reads at a nice even pace, and does all the different voices perfectly, IMHO. Great performance! <br /><br />I definitely recommend this series for anyone who enjoys urban fantasy. Jim Butcher weaves in a lot of action, humor and grit. Ignore the television series from a few years ago -- it was Crap (with a capital C). The books are SO much better!! <br /><br />On to book #11 -- Turn Coat! The series has 15 books so far....with #16 Peace Talks coming soon. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8345218181632254420">Another great entry in the series. The war with the Red Court might have cooled down temporarily but Harry has peeved off quite a few nasties so far in the series and a lot of them come back round to bite him in the ass.   <span id="freeText8345218181632254420" style="display:none">Another great entry in the series. Great audio narration from James Marsters as usual.<br /><br />Plenty of action this book starting from the first few minutes. The war with the Red Court might have cooled down temporarily but Harry has peeved off quite a few nasties so far in the series and a lot of them come back round to bite him in the ass. Good thing it's tough as leather. Or at least it's covered with leather infused with magic shielding. <br /><br />It's a bit hard to review this one because mentioning the biggest baddest baddies on the block is spoilery. We've seen them before. Apart from them we have the Faerie courts involved. We have Gruffs - yes, as in Billy goats gruff. Which means they can kill trolls, which means when they come gunning for Harry it's time to scramble.<br /><br />Some favourite characters that feature include Kincaid, Michael, Sanya (I just dig Marsters Russian mafia accent), Murphy of course, Luccio and more. So Harry has plenty of backup. And he'll need them because when Mab comes to collect on one of the favors Harry owes her she doesn't take no for an answer. The whole "I'll only do those favors I choose" routine isn't going to work this time. <br /><br />Lots of interesting plot elements, some new characters, some new creatures, some intense battle scenes, and Harry levels up. Very nice.<br /><br /><br />4 stars</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1332042003?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>

        rated it

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=paranormal-mystery">paranormal-mystery</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1332042003" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2467472852133582812">The very first thing I have to say about this book is: How in the world do people live in places where it snows? I mean, the descriptions in this book of living in a place with snow during the winter sounds soooooo miserable! I can't even imagine having to dig my car out of ice, or shovel my walkway in order to leave my house each day. You people must be insane or something!<br/><br/><a href='http://photobucket.com/images/snow' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436851293i/15510770.gif' alt='snow photo: tired of snow ? its_snow_funny.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><i>this would be me at the airport upon landing in the place where there is snow</i><br/><br/>Harry needs to move to the South. His long</span>
  <span id="freeText2467472852133582812" style="display:none">The very first thing I have to say about this book is: How in the world do people live in places where it snows? I mean, the descriptions in this book of living in a place with snow during the winter sounds soooooo miserable! I can't even imagine having to dig my car out of ice, or shovel my walkway in order to leave my house each day. You people must be insane or something!<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/snow" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436851293i/15510770.gif" alt="snow photo: tired of snow ? its_snow_funny.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>this would be me at the airport upon landing in the place where there is snow</i><br><br>Harry needs to move to the South. His long coat and cowboy boots would fit in better here too. Plus, we like guns. They pretty much give you a gun in your welcome basket upon moving to Texas. It's our thing.<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/texas%20guns" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436851293i/15510771.gif" alt="texas guns photo: chimpanzee-glock.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>Even our zoo animals are armed here...</i><br><br>Even Harry recognizes that it's our thing:<br><b>
  <i>He had enough guns strapped to his body to outfit a terrorist cell, or a Texan nuclear family...</i>
</b><br><br>Murphy and Kincaid would love it here!<br><br>On to the book! So, in a previous book, many books ago, Harry had to make a deal with Mab, Queen of the Winter Fae Unseelie Court, to win his freedom back from a stupid deal he made in his childhood. He had to promise her three favors. He did one, and owes her two. Well, it's time to open door number two: find and free the local gangster, Johnnie Marcone, from his kidnappers. Sounds easy enough, huh? Hahaha! Nothing is ever easy for Harry! He is the king of Murphy's Law.<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/murphy%27s%20law" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436851293i/15510772.jpg" alt="murphy's law photo: law.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So, things get complicated, Harry makes a bunch of smartass remarks, Thomas looks beautiful, Murphy is a badass, Molly sneaks in, Bob says something smarmy, and lots of people get hurt........the end....<br><br>What I am really hoping for is for Butcher to break the meta at this point. I like the books, and I'm okay if they stay the same, but I'm hoping for a really big shake-up somewhere down the line. That would be pretty cool.</span>

<div id="review_1234621455" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1234621455" />
    <a title="Deborah Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/954028-deborah-markus"><img alt="Deborah Markus" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1234621455?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Markus" href="/user/show/954028-deborah-markus">Deborah Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/954028-deborah-markus?shelf=library-find">library-find</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1234621455" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9711753910619244327">Note the five stars and take what follows for what it's worth.<br/><br/>I'm a few books ahead -- I'm just behind on posting. But this book, and another one to come, confirmed what I began to suspect a book or two ago, which is that Jim Butcher has developed a poker tell.<br/><br/>I don't want to say much or I'll spoil the suspense for you the way Butcher has started to for me. I'll try to be vague enough that you won't know what I mean until you finish the book, look back with this review in mind, and get it. Maybe</span>
  <span id="freeText9711753910619244327" style="display:none">Note the five stars and take what follows for what it's worth.<br /><br />I'm a few books ahead -- I'm just behind on posting. But this book, and another one to come, confirmed what I began to suspect a book or two ago, which is that Jim Butcher has developed a poker tell.<br /><br />I don't want to say much or I'll spoil the suspense for you the way Butcher has started to for me. I'll try to be vague enough that you won't know what I mean until you finish the book, look back with this review in mind, and get it. Maybe you won't agree. Either way, I'd love to chat about this with a Dresden fan. <br /><br />Harry Dresden is a fully-developed character -- a human on the page, as it will. Prick him and he bleeds and all that.<br /><br />Except.<br /><br />Except he's starting not to respond to events the way I've so far been able to count on him responding. The guy started off one of his own novels being physically ill because he was upset by the violence he'd just witnessed. He's not Clint Eastwood, nor does he want to be.<br /><br />I hate being kept in suspense too long as much as any reader, but I'm annoyed that I'm starting to say, "Oh, wait -- it's going to be okay" long before I've been given official word that things are, in fact, okay.<br /><br />If you've read the series -- the whole series, not just up to this book -- go ahead and read the spoiler below. If you haven't read the series but think you might, DON'T read the spoiler, because it turns out that word is entirely accurate.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Harry Dresden didn't react at all to the fact that he'd witnessed his dog being murdered a book or two ago, and that's how I knew his dog was somehow actually okay. He had the same utter lack of reaction when he saw Michael shot in a way that should have meant the end of Michael. And hey, look! Jokey-jokey time right after Butters takes a well-aimed bullet from a professional killer, and guess who's okay after all? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Somebody tell Butcher that he keeps giving his hand away. I'm very surprised his agent and/or editor haven't caught this tell, but it's real and it's kind of a bummer to hardcore nerd readers like me.<br /><br />He still gets five stars, though, because he's still doing everything else right.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9711753910619244327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike&#39;s Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike&#39;s Book Reviews" href="/user/show/59173659-mike-s-book-reviews">Mike&#39;s Book Reviews</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451462008" href="/book/show/3456594-small-favor">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3196221324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3457001704286153406">Full Video Review Here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://youtu.be/rVlYaimtnNA'>https://youtu.be/rVlYaimtnNA</a><br/><br/>After having some mixed opinions on White Night, this book was exactly the shot in the arm I needed to get recharged on the series going forward. With the return of the Denarians and my favorite series Big Bad, as well as my favorite supporting characters in the Knights of the Cross, this almost felt like the direct sequel to Death Masks (my favorite book in the series thus far).<br/><br/>The grading curve I use for these books are villain, case, and sup</span>
  <span id="freeText3457001704286153406" style="display:none">Full Video Review Here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/rVlYaimtnNA">https://youtu.be/rVlYaimtnNA</a><br /><br />After having some mixed opinions on White Night, this book was exactly the shot in the arm I needed to get recharged on the series going forward. With the return of the Denarians and my favorite series Big Bad, as well as my favorite supporting characters in the Knights of the Cross, this almost felt like the direct sequel to Death Masks (my favorite book in the series thus far).<br /><br />The grading curve I use for these books are villain, case, and supporting cast. This one nails all three of those requirements as Harry looks to help Michael and the Knights rid humanity of the Denarians and their coins once and for all.The return of Ivy, Kincaid, Sanya, and other familiar faces helped Butcher to continue building this fascinating world he has created without anything feeling formulaic.<br /><br />While everything with the Fae continue to (intentionally) confusing, the case is a compelling one since it deals with a personal fave in gentleman Johnny Marcone. Butcher taking a spin of classic fairy tale creatures like the Three Billy Goats Gruff is always amusing in a way that continues to give Dresden Files the charm it has become famous for. Just a fun ride that is in the upper third of my first 10 Harry Dresden adventures.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/24529785-small-favor">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2681923870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2345986611896758402">After the events of White Night, it was nice to hear Harry has had a relatively quiet year. Time to spend with his brother, friends and preparing his young apprentice but all that is about to change when Mab, monarch of the Sidhe Winter Court, calls in an old favor from Harry.<br/><br/>Narrated by James Marsters this tale comes to life through his narration. From the voices, to his able to make you feel each characters' emotions it has been delightful listening to Marsters become a masterful narrator. <br/>I k</span>
  <span id="freeText2345986611896758402" style="display:none">After the events of White Night, it was nice to hear Harry has had a relatively quiet year. Time to spend with his brother, friends and preparing his young apprentice but all that is about to change when Mab, monarch of the Sidhe Winter Court, calls in an old favor from Harry.<br /><br />Narrated by James Marsters this tale comes to life through his narration. From the voices, to his able to make you feel each characters' emotions it has been delightful listening to Marsters become a masterful narrator. <br />I know I say this all the time, but hands to God, this series gets better with every book. From the nail-biting pace to the favor they task Harry with, there are twists and turns, betrayals, revelations and a lot of kickassary.<br /><br />Mobster kingpin Johnny Marcone has been kidnapped by those in the supernatural world and Mab wants him found. And everyone is taking sides which causes danger for Harry and the friends he enlists to aid him. Denizens of the Summer Court attack, the Order of the Blackened Denarias want the Archive and so much more.<br /><br />Harry enlists the Knights of the Cross, Murphy, Thomas, Molly and Kincaid to aid him. He also gains help from a talking skull whom I happen to love. Humor, tests of friendship and more await you! While the threads are action packed, I also felt like Butcher was using this as a bridge book. It will test Harry's friendship with Michael as Molly matures.<br /><br />While the story is far from perfect and a time or two, I needed to re-listen to a section to keep up there is no doubt Butcher is a tremendous storyteller. Together with Marsters are narrator they weave magic. I lost track of time, laughed aloud and simple enjoy!<a href="https://caffeinatedbookreviewer.com/2019/02/small-favor-by-jim-butcher.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> This review was originally posted at Caffeinated Reviewer</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2345986611896758402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
